I've uploaded a code repository in the directory /testbed. Consider the following PR description:

<pr_description>
BUG | `onClickOutside` | Detecting iFrame clicks fails if the iFrame is within a custom element Shadow DOM, even when enabling `detectIframe` option
### Describe the bug

`onClickOutside` doesn't trigger when clicking an iframe which is wrapped in a custom element within a Shadow DOM, even if `detectIframe` is enabled.
This is because `detectIframe` actually verifies that the activeElement is an iFrame so it won't detect clicks in custom elements. I confirmed that the window `blur` event is indeed firing when clicking the iframe, but onClickOutside is not triggering.

Could the check be made broader, to trigger any time the window loses focus?

### Reproduction

https://stackblitz.com/edit/vitejs-vite-jcsqmkbs?file=src%2FApp.vue

    12	  /**
    13	   * List of elements that should not trigger the event,
    14	   * provided as Refs or CSS Selectors.

    16	  ignore?: MaybeRefOrGetter<(MaybeElementRef | string)[]>

    78	// Implementation
    79	export function onClickOutside(
    80	  target: MaybeComputedElementRef,
    81	  handler: OnClickOutsideHandler,
    82	  options: OnClickOutsideOptions<boolean> = {},
    83	): OnClickOutsideReturn<boolean> {
    84	  const { window = defaultWindow, ignore = [], capture = true, detectIframe = false, controls = false } = options
    85	
    86	  if (!window) {
    87	    return controls
    88	      ? { stop: noop, cancel: noop, trigger: noop }
    89	      : noop
    90	  }
    91	
    92	  // Fixes: https://github.com/vueuse/vueuse/issues/1520
    93	  // How it works: https://stackoverflow.com/a/39712411
    94	  if (isIOS && !_iOSWorkaround) {
    95	    _iOSWorkaround = true
    96	    const listenerOptions = { passive: true }
    97	    // Not using useEventListener because these event handlers must not be disposed.
    98	    // See previously linked references and https://github.com/vueuse/vueuse/issues/4724
    99	    Array.from(window.document.body.children)
   100	      .forEach(el => el.addEventListener('click', noop, listenerOptions))
   101	    window.document.documentElement.addEventListener('click', noop, listenerOptions)
   102	  }
   103	
   104	  let shouldListen = true
   105	
   106	  const shouldIgnore = (event: Event) => {
   107	    return toValue(ignore).some((target) => {
   108	      if (typeof target === 'string') {
   109	        return Array.from(window.document.querySelectorAll(target))
   110	          .some(el => el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   111	      }
   112	      else {
   113	        const el = unrefElement(target)
   114	        return el && (event.target === el || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   115	      }
   116	    })
   117	  }
   118	
   119	  /**
   120	   * Determines if the given target has multiple root elements.
   121	   * Referenced from: https://github.com/vuejs/test-utils/blob/ccb460be55f9f6be05ab708500a41ec8adf6f4bc/src/vue-wrapper.ts#L21
   122	   */
   123	  function hasMultipleRoots(target: MaybeComputedElementRef): boolean {
   124	    const vm = toValue(target) as ComponentPublicInstance
   125	    return vm && vm.$.subTree.shapeFlag === 16
   126	  }
   127	
   128	  function checkMultipleRoots(target: MaybeComputedElementRef, event: Event): boolean {
   129	    const vm = toValue(target) as ComponentPublicInstance
   130	    const children = vm.$.subTree && vm.$.subTree.children
   131	
   132	    if (children == null || !Array.isArray(children))
   133	      return false
   134	
   135	    // @ts-expect-error should be VNode
   136	    return children.some((child: VNode) => child.el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(child.el))
   137	  }
   138	
   139	  const listener = (event: Event) => {
   140	    const el = unrefElement(target)
   141	
   142	    if (event.target == null)
   143	      return
   144	
   145	    if (!(el instanceof Element) && hasMultipleRoots(target) && checkMultipleRoots(target, event))
   146	      return
   147	
   148	    if (!el || el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   149	      return
   150	
   151	    if ('detail' in event && event.detail === 0)
   152	      shouldListen = !shouldIgnore(event)
   153	
   154	    if (!shouldListen) {
   155	      shouldListen = true
   156	      return
   157	    }
   158	
   159	    handler(event as any)
   160	  }
   161	
   162	  let isProcessingClick = false
   163	
   164	  const cleanup = [
   165	    useEventListener(window, 'click', (event: PointerEvent) => {
   166	      if (!isProcessingClick) {
   167	        isProcessingClick = true
   168	        setTimeout(() => {
   169	          isProcessingClick = false
   170	        }, 0)
   171	        listener(event)
   172	      }
   173	    }, { passive: true, capture }),
   174	    useEventListener(window, 'pointerdown', (e) => {
   175	      const el = unrefElement(target)
   176	      shouldListen = !shouldIgnore(e) && !!(el && !e.composedPath().includes(el))
   177	    }, { passive: true }),
   178	    detectIframe && useEventListener(window, 'blur', (event) => {
   179	      setTimeout(() => {
   180	        const el = unrefElement(target)
   181	        if (
   182	          window.document.activeElement?.tagName === 'IFRAME'
   183	          && !el?.contains(window.document.activeElement)
   184	        ) {
   185	          handler(event as any)
   186	        }
   187	      }, 0)
   188	    }, { passive: true }),
   189	  ].filter(Boolean) as Fn[]
   190	
   191	  const stop = () => cleanup.forEach(fn => fn())
   192	
   193	  if (controls) {
   194	    return {
   195	      stop,
   196	      cancel: () => {
   197	        shouldListen = false
   198	      },
   199	      trigger: (event: Event) => {
   200	        shouldListen = true
   201	        listener(event)
   202	        shouldListen = false
   203	      },
   204	    }
   205	  }
   206	
   207	  return stop
   208	}

```javascript

  if (el.tagName === 'IFRAME') return true;
  if (el.shadowRoot?.activeElement) {
    return containsIframe(el.shadowRoot.activeElement);
  }
  // Also check all children? That could be expensive.
  return false;
}
```

But actually, using `activeElement` on the shadow root is the right approach because we're tracking where focus went.

   188	            if (document.activeElement !== activeElement) {
   189	              // We traversed into shadow DOM; check the original active element (the shadow host)
   190	              if (!el?.contains(document.activeElement)) {
   191	                handler(event as any)
   192	              }
   193	            }
   194	            else {
   195	              // The iframe is directly the active element
   196	              if (!el?.contains(activeElement)) {
   197	                handler(event as any)
   198	              }
   199	            }
   200	            break
   201	          }
   202	          // Check if the active element is a shadow host whose focus is inside its shadow DOM
   203	          if (activeElement.shadowRoot) {
   204	            activeElement = activeElement.shadowRoot.activeElement
   205	          }
   206	          else {
   207	            break
   208	          }
   209	        }
   210	      }, 0)
   211	    }, { passive: true }),
   212	  ].filter(Boolean) as Fn[]
   213	
   214	  const stop = () => cleanup.forEach(fn => fn())

    12	  /**
    13	   * List of elements that should not trigger the event,
    14	   * provided as Refs or CSS Selectors.
    15	   */
    16	  ignore?: MaybeRefOrGetter<(MaybeElementRef | string)[]>
    17	  /**
    18	   * Use capturing phase for internal event listener.
    19	   * @default true
    20	   */

    23	   * Run handler function if focus moves to an iframe.
    24	   * @default false
    25	   */

    27	  /**
    28	   * Use controls to cancel/trigger listener.
    29	   * @default false
    30	   */

    35	  T extends OnClickOutsideOptions<boolean> = OnClickOutsideOptions,

    51	 * Listen for clicks outside of an element.

    77	
    78	// Implementation
    79	export function onClickOutside(
    80	  target: MaybeComputedElementRef,
    81	  handler: OnClickOutsideHandler,
    82	  options: OnClickOutsideOptions<boolean> = {},
    83	): OnClickOutsideReturn<boolean> {
    84	  const { window = defaultWindow, ignore = [], capture = true, detectIframe = false, controls = false } = options
    85	
    86	  if (!window) {
    87	    return controls
    88	      ? { stop: noop, cancel: noop, trigger: noop }
    89	      : noop
    90	  }
    91	
    92	  // Fixes: https://github.com/vueuse/vueuse/issues/1520
    93	  // How it works: https://stackoverflow.com/a/39712411
    94	  if (isIOS && !_iOSWorkaround) {
    95	    _iOSWorkaround = true
    96	    const listenerOptions = { passive: true }
    97	    // Not using useEventListener because these event handlers must not be disposed.
    98	    // See previously linked references and https://github.com/vueuse/vueuse/issues/4724
    99	    Array.from(window.document.body.children)
   100	      .forEach(el => el.addEventListener('click', noop, listenerOptions))
   101	    window.document.documentElement.addEventListener('click', noop, listenerOptions)
   102	  }
   103	
   104	  let shouldListen = true
   105	
   106	  const shouldIgnore = (event: Event) => {
   107	    return toValue(ignore).some((target) => {
   108	      if (typeof target === 'string') {
   109	        return Array.from(window.document.querySelectorAll(target))
   110	          .some(el => el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   111	      }
   112	      else {
   113	        const el = unrefElement(target)
   114	        return el && (event.target === el || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   115	      }
   116	    })
   117	  }
   118	
   119	  /**
   120	   * Determines if the given target has multiple root elements.
   121	   * Referenced from: https://github.com/vuejs/test-utils/blob/ccb460be55f9f6be05ab708500a41ec8adf6f4bc/src/vue-wrapper.ts#L21
   122	   */
   123	  function hasMultipleRoots(target: MaybeComputedElementRef): boolean {
   124	    const vm = toValue(target) as ComponentPublicInstance
   125	    return vm && vm.$.subTree.shapeFlag === 16
   126	  }
   127	
   128	  function checkMultipleRoots(target: MaybeComputedElementRef, event: Event): boolean {
   129	    const vm = toValue(target) as ComponentPublicInstance
   130	    const children = vm.$.subTree && vm.$.subTree.children
   131	
   132	    if (children == null || !Array.isArray(children))
   133	      return false
   134	
   135	    // @ts-expect-error should be VNode
   136	    return children.some((child: VNode) => child.el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(child.el))
   137	  }
   138	
   139	  const listener = (event: Event) => {
   140	    const el = unrefElement(target)
   141	
   142	    if (event.target == null)
   143	      return
   144	
   145	    if (!(el instanceof Element) && hasMultipleRoots(target) && checkMultipleRoots(target, event))
   146	      return
   147	
   148	    if (!el || el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   149	      return
   150	
   151	    if ('detail' in event && event.detail === 0)
   152	      shouldListen = !shouldIgnore(event)
   153	
   154	    if (!shouldListen) {
   155	      shouldListen = true
   156	      return
   157	    }
   158	
   159	    handler(event as any)
   160	  }
   161	
   162	  let isProcessingClick = false
   163	
   164	  const cleanup = [
   165	    useEventListener(window, 'click', (event: PointerEvent) => {
   166	      if (!isProcessingClick) {
   167	        isProcessingClick = true
   168	        setTimeout(() => {
   169	          isProcessingClick = false
   170	        }, 0)
   171	        listener(event)
   172	      }
   173	    }, { passive: true, capture }),
   174	    useEventListener(window, 'pointerdown', (e) => {
   175	      const el = unrefElement(target)
   176	      shouldListen = !shouldIgnore(e) && !!(el && !e.composedPath().includes(el))
   177	    }, { passive: true }),
   178	    detectIframe && useEventListener(window, 'blur', (event) => {
   179	      setTimeout(() => {
   180	        const el = unrefElement(target)
   181	        // Traverse activeElement chain to find iframe, including through shadow DOMs
   182	        let activeElement: Element | null = document.activeElement
   183	        while (activeElement) {
   184	          if (activeElement.tagName === 'IFRAME') {
   185	            // Check if the iframe (or its ancestor shadow host) is contained in the target element
   186	            // document.activeElement is the top-level element; if it's within the target,
   187	            // then the iframe is also within the target (even if in shadow DOM)
   188	            if (document.activeElement !== activeElement) {
   189	              // We traversed into shadow DOM; check the original active element (the shadow host)
   190	              if (!el?.contains(document.activeElement)) {
   191	                handler(event as any)
   192	              }
   193	            }
   194	            else {
   195	              // The iframe is directly the active element
   196	              if (!el?.contains(activeElement)) {
   197	                handler(event as any)
   198	              }
   199	            }
   200	            break
   201	          }
   202	          // Check if the active element is a shadow host whose focus is inside its shadow DOM
   203	          if (activeElement.shadowRoot) {
   204	            activeElement = activeElement.shadowRoot.activeElement
   205	          }
   206	          else {
   207	            break
   208	          }
   209	        }
   210	      }, 0)
   211	    }, { passive: true }),
   212	  ].filter(Boolean) as Fn[]
   213	
   214	  const stop = () => cleanup.forEach(fn => fn())
   215	
   216	  if (controls) {
   217	    return {
   218	      stop,
   219	      cancel: () => {
   220	        shouldListen = false
   221	      },
   222	      trigger: (event: Event) => {
   223	        shouldListen = true
   224	        listener(event)
   225	        shouldListen = false
   226	      },
   227	    }
   228	  }
   229	
   230	  return stop
   231	}

     1	import type { OnClickOutsideHandler, OnClickOutsideOptions } from '@vueuse/core'
     2	import type { Fn } from '@vueuse/shared'
     3	import type { ObjectDirective } from 'vue'
     4	import { onClickOutside } from '@vueuse/core'
     5	
     6	type StopHandle = Fn | { stop: Fn, cancel: Fn, trigger: (event: Event) => void }
     7	
     8	const stopClickOutsideMap = new WeakMap<HTMLElement, StopHandle>()
     9	
    10	export const vOnClickOutside: ObjectDirective<
    11	  HTMLElement,
    12	  OnClickOutsideHandler | [(evt: any) => void, Omit<OnClickOutsideOptions, 'controls'>]
    13	> = {
    14	  mounted(el, binding) {
    15	    const capture = !binding.modifiers.bubble
    16	    let stop: StopHandle
    17	    if (typeof binding.value === 'function') {
    18	      stop = onClickOutside(el, binding.value, { capture })
    19	    }
    20	    else {
    21	      const [handler, options] = binding.value
    22	      stop = onClickOutside(el, handler, Object.assign({ capture }, options))
    23	    }
    24	    stopClickOutsideMap.set(el, stop)
    25	  },
    26	  unmounted(el) {
    27	    const stop = stopClickOutsideMap.get(el)
    28	    if (stop && typeof stop === 'function') {
    29	      stop()
    30	    }
    31	    else {
    32	      stop?.stop()
    33	    }
    34	    stopClickOutsideMap.delete(el)
    35	  },
    36	}
    37	
    38	/** @deprecated use `vOnClickOutside` instead */
    39	export const VOnClickOutside = vOnClickOutside

Now let me think about edge cases more thoroughly:

1. **Direct iframe (original case)**: `document.activeElement` is an `IFRAME`. My code enters the while loop, checks `activeElement.tagName === 'IFRAME'` → true. Since `document.activeElement === activeElement` (both are the same iframe), it goes to the else branch and checks `!el?.contains(activeElement)`. This is the same as the original behavior. ✓

2. **Iframe inside a custom element with Shadow DOM (new case)**: `document.activeElement` is the custom element (shadow host). The loop:
   - Iteration 1: `activeElement` = custom element. `tagName !== 'IFRAME'`. `activeElement.shadowRoot` exists → `activeElement = shadowRoot.activeElement` (the iframe).
   - Iteration 2: `activeElement` = iframe. `tagName === 'IFRAME'` → true. `document.activeElement !== activeElement` (custom element ≠ iframe) → checks `!el?.contains(document.activeElement)` (i.e., is the custom element outside the target?). ✓

3. **Nested shadow DOMs**: `document.activeElement` = outer custom element. Loop traverses through multiple shadow roots until finding the iframe. The containment check uses `document.activeElement` (the outermost element). This is correct because if the outermost custom element is inside the target, the iframe is also inside the target. ✓

4. **No iframe involved**: `document.activeElement` is some other element (e.g., a button). The loop:
   - Iteration 1: `tagName !== 'IFRAME'`. If it has a shadow root, it traverses. Eventually either finds an iframe or exhausts the chain. If no iframe is found, the handler is not called. ✓

5. **Null/undefined activeElement**: The while loop condition `while (activeElement)` handles null. If `document.activeElement` is null, the loop body never executes. ✓

This looks solid. But wait, there's another potential issue: the original code also had `window.document.activeElement` (with `window.`) while my code uses `document.activeElement`. Let me check if `window` here refers to the parameter (which could be a custom window).

Looking at the code:
- Line 84: `const { window = defaultWindow, ... } = options`
- The original code used `window.document.activeElement`

But in my changes, I used `document.activeElement` instead of `window.document.activeElement`. This could be a problem if the user passes a custom window (e.g., for iframe scenarios). Let me fix that:

            // document.activeElement is the top-level element; if it'"'"'s within the target,
            // then the iframe is also within the target (even if in shadow DOM)

              // We traversed into shadow DOM; check the original active element (the shadow host)

                handler(event as any)

    11	export interface OnClickOutsideOptions<Controls extends boolean = false> extends ConfigurableWindow {
    12	  /**
    13	   * List of elements that should not trigger the event,
    14	   * provided as Refs or CSS Selectors.
    15	   */
    16	  ignore?: MaybeRefOrGetter<(MaybeElementRef | string)[]>
    17	  /**
    18	   * Use capturing phase for internal event listener.
    19	   * @default true
    20	   */
    21	  capture?: boolean
    22	  /**
    23	   * Run handler function if focus moves to an iframe.
    24	   * @default false
    25	   */
    26	  detectIframe?: boolean
    27	  /**
    28	   * Use controls to cancel/trigger listener.
    29	   * @default false
    30	   */
    31	  controls?: Controls
    32	}

    34	export type OnClickOutsideHandler<
    35	  T extends OnClickOutsideOptions<boolean> = OnClickOutsideOptions,
    36	> = (
    37	  event: (T['detectIframe'] extends true ? FocusEvent : never)
    38	    | (T['controls'] extends true ? Event : never)
    39	    | PointerEvent,

    43	  stop: Fn

    51	 * Listen for clicks outside of an element.

    53	 * @see https://vueuse.org/onClickOutside

    73	  stop: Fn

    77	
    78	// Implementation
    79	export function onClickOutside(
    80	  target: MaybeComputedElementRef,
    81	  handler: OnClickOutsideHandler,
    82	  options: OnClickOutsideOptions<boolean> = {},
    83	): OnClickOutsideReturn<boolean> {
    84	  const { window = defaultWindow, ignore = [], capture = true, detectIframe = false, controls = false } = options
    85	
    86	  if (!window) {
    87	    return controls
    88	      ? { stop: noop, cancel: noop, trigger: noop }
    89	      : noop
    90	  }
    91	
    92	  // Fixes: https://github.com/vueuse/vueuse/issues/1520
    93	  // How it works: https://stackoverflow.com/a/39712411
    94	  if (isIOS && !_iOSWorkaround) {
    95	    _iOSWorkaround = true
    96	    const listenerOptions = { passive: true }
    97	    // Not using useEventListener because these event handlers must not be disposed.
    98	    // See previously linked references and https://github.com/vueuse/vueuse/issues/4724
    99	    Array.from(window.document.body.children)
   100	      .forEach(el => el.addEventListener('click', noop, listenerOptions))
   101	    window.document.documentElement.addEventListener('click', noop, listenerOptions)
   102	  }
   103	
   104	  let shouldListen = true
   105	
   106	  const shouldIgnore = (event: Event) => {
   107	    return toValue(ignore).some((target) => {
   108	      if (typeof target === 'string') {
   109	        return Array.from(window.document.querySelectorAll(target))
   110	          .some(el => el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   111	      }
   112	      else {
   113	        const el = unrefElement(target)
   114	        return el && (event.target === el || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   115	      }
   116	    })
   117	  }
   118	
   119	  /**
   120	   * Determines if the given target has multiple root elements.
   121	   * Referenced from: https://github.com/vuejs/test-utils/blob/ccb460be55f9f6be05ab708500a41ec8adf6f4bc/src/vue-wrapper.ts#L21
   122	   */
   123	  function hasMultipleRoots(target: MaybeComputedElementRef): boolean {
   124	    const vm = toValue(target) as ComponentPublicInstance
   125	    return vm && vm.$.subTree.shapeFlag === 16
   126	  }
   127	
   128	  function checkMultipleRoots(target: MaybeComputedElementRef, event: Event): boolean {
   129	    const vm = toValue(target) as ComponentPublicInstance
   130	    const children = vm.$.subTree && vm.$.subTree.children
   131	
   132	    if (children == null || !Array.isArray(children))
   133	      return false
   134	
   135	    // @ts-expect-error should be VNode
   136	    return children.some((child: VNode) => child.el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(child.el))
   137	  }
   138	
   139	  const listener = (event: Event) => {
   140	    const el = unrefElement(target)
   141	
   142	    if (event.target == null)
   143	      return
   144	
   145	    if (!(el instanceof Element) && hasMultipleRoots(target) && checkMultipleRoots(target, event))
   146	      return
   147	
   148	    if (!el || el === event.target || event.composedPath().includes(el))
   149	      return
   150	
   151	    if ('detail' in event && event.detail === 0)
   152	      shouldListen = !shouldIgnore(event)
   153	
   154	    if (!shouldListen) {
   155	      shouldListen = true
   156	      return
   157	    }
   158	
   159	    handler(event as any)
   160	  }
   161	
   162	  let isProcessingClick = false
   163	
   164	  const cleanup = [
   165	    useEventListener(window, 'click', (event: PointerEvent) => {
   166	      if (!isProcessingClick) {
   167	        isProcessingClick = true
   168	        setTimeout(() => {
   169	          isProcessingClick = false
   170	        }, 0)
   171	        listener(event)
   172	      }
   173	    }, { passive: true, capture }),
   174	    useEventListener(window, 'pointerdown', (e) => {
   175	      const el = unrefElement(target)
   176	      shouldListen = !shouldIgnore(e) && !!(el && !e.composedPath().includes(el))
   177	    }, { passive: true }),
   178	    detectIframe && useEventListener(window, 'blur', (event) => {
   179	      setTimeout(() => {
   180	        const el = unrefElement(target)
   181	        // Traverse activeElement chain to find iframe, including through shadow DOMs
   182	        const { document: doc } = window
   183	        let activeElement: Element | null = doc.activeElement
   184	        while (activeElement) {
   185	          if (activeElement.tagName === 'IFRAME') {
   186	            // Check if the iframe (or its ancestor shadow host) is contained in the target element
   187	            // doc.activeElement is the top-level element; if it's within the target,
   188	            // then the iframe is also within the target (even if in shadow DOM)
   189	            if (doc.activeElement !== activeElement) {
   190	              // We traversed into shadow DOM; check the original active element (the shadow host)
   191	              if (!el?.contains(doc.activeElement)) {
   192	                handler(event as any)
   193	              }
   194	            }
   195	            else {
   196	              // The iframe is directly the active element
   197	              if (!el?.contains(activeElement)) {
   198	                handler(event as any)
   199	              }
   200	            }
   201	            break
   202	          }
   203	          // Check if the active element is a shadow host whose focus is inside its shadow DOM
   204	          if (activeElement.shadowRoot) {
   205	            activeElement = activeElement.shadowRoot.activeElement
   206	          }
   207	          else {
   208	            break
   209	          }
   210	        }
   211	      }, 0)
   212	    }, { passive: true }),
   213	  ].filter(Boolean) as Fn[]
   214	
   215	  const stop = () => cleanup.forEach(fn => fn())
   216	
   217	  if (controls) {
   218	    return {
   219	      stop,
   220	      cancel: () => {
   221	        shouldListen = false
   222	      },
   223	      trigger: (event: Event) => {
   224	        shouldListen = true
   225	        listener(event)
   226	        shouldListen = false
   227	      },
   228	    }
   229	  }
   230	
   231	  return stop
   232	}

Now let me think about whether there's anything else I should consider. Let me look at the PR description again:

> `onClickOutside` doesn't trigger when clicking an iframe which is wrapped in a custom element within a Shadow DOM, even if `detectIframe` is enabled.
> This is because `detectIframe` actually verifies that the activeElement is an iFrame so it won't detect clicks in custom elements.

My fix addresses this by traversing the shadow DOM to find if the actual focused element is an iframe, even when it's nested within one or more shadow roots.

> Could the check be made broader, to trigger any time the window loses focus?

While my fix doesn't go as far as triggering on *any* window blur, it does broaden the check to handle the shadow DOM case. Triggering on any blur would be too aggressive (it would fire when clicking the address bar, switching tabs, etc.). The current approach of checking that the focus actually went to an iframe is the right behavior; we just need to also detect iframes that are inside shadow DOMs.

     1	import type { ShallowRef } from 'vue'
     2	import type { ConfigurableDocumentOrShadowRoot, ConfigurableWindow } from '../_configurable'
     3	import { shallowRef } from 'vue'
     4	import { defaultWindow } from '../_configurable'
     5	import { onElementRemoval } from '../onElementRemoval'
     6	import { useEventListener } from '../useEventListener'
     7	
     8	export interface UseActiveElementOptions extends ConfigurableWindow, ConfigurableDocumentOrShadowRoot {
     9	  /**
    10	   * Search active element deeply inside shadow dom
    11	   *
    12	   * @default true
    13	   */
    14	  deep?: boolean
    15	  /**
    16	   * Track active element when it's removed from the DOM
    17	   * Using a MutationObserver under the hood
    18	   * @default false
    19	   */
    20	  triggerOnRemoval?: boolean
    21	}
    22	
    23	export type UseActiveElementReturn<T extends HTMLElement = HTMLElement> = ShallowRef<T | null | undefined>
    24	
    25	/**
    26	 * Reactive `document.activeElement`
    27	 *
    28	 * @see https://vueuse.org/useActiveElement
    29	 * @param options
    30	 *
    31	 * @__NO_SIDE_EFFECTS__
    32	 */
    33	export function useActiveElement<T extends HTMLElement>(
    34	  options: UseActiveElementOptions = {},
    35	): UseActiveElementReturn<T> {
    36	  const {
    37	    window = defaultWindow,
    38	    deep = true,
    39	    triggerOnRemoval = false,
    40	  } = options
    41	  const document = options.document ?? window?.document
    42	
    43	  const getDeepActiveElement = () => {
    44	    let element = document?.activeElement
    45	    if (deep) {
    46	      while (element?.shadowRoot)
    47	        element = element?.shadowRoot?.activeElement
    48	    }
    49	    return element
    50	  }
    51	
    52	  const activeElement = shallowRef<T | null | undefined>()
    53	  const trigger = () => {
    54	    activeElement.value = getDeepActiveElement() as T | null | undefined
    55	  }
    56	
    57	  if (window) {
    58	    const listenerOptions = {
    59	      capture: true,
    60	      passive: true,
    61	    }
    62	
    63	    useEventListener(
    64	      window,
    65	      'blur',
    66	      (event) => {
    67	        if (event.relatedTarget !== null)
    68	          return
    69	        trigger()
    70	      },
    71	      listenerOptions,
    72	    )
    73	    useEventListener(
    74	      window,
    75	      'focus',
    76	      trigger,
    77	      listenerOptions,
    78	    )
    79	  }
    80	
    81	  if (triggerOnRemoval) {
    82	    onElementRemoval(activeElement, trigger, { document })
    83	  }
    84	
    85	  trigger()
    86	
    87	  return activeElement
    88	}

This is very helpful. The `useActiveElement` has a `getDeepActiveElement` function that does exactly what I implemented: it traverses shadow DOMs via `shadowRoot.activeElement`. My implementation is consistent with this pattern.

However, I notice a subtle difference: `useActiveElement` uses a while loop that traverses as long as there's a `shadowRoot`, while my implementation checks for `tagName === 'IFRAME'` at each level. Both are valid, but my approach is more specific to finding iframes.

 </template>
 ```
 
+### Using Component
+
+```vue
+<script setup lang="ts">
+import { UseSortable } from '@vueuse/integrations/useSortable/component'
+import { shallowRef } from 'vue'
+
+const list = shallowRef([
+  { id: 1, name: 'a' },
+  { id: 2, name: 'b' },
+  { id: 3, name: 'c' },
+])
+</script>
+
+<template>
+  <UseSortable v-model="list" as="ol" :options="{ animation: 150 }">
+    <li v-for="item in list" :key="item.id">
+      {{ item.name }}
+    </li>
+  </UseSortable>
+</template>
+```
+
+You can also access the helper functions like `start`, `stop`, and `option` from the slot scope:
+
+```vue
+<template>
+  <UseSortable v-slot="{ stop, start }" v-model="list">
+    <button @click="stop()">
+      Stop Sorting
+    </button>
+    <button @click="start()">
+      Start Sorting
+    </button>
+    <div v-for="item in list" :key="item.id">
+      {{ item.name }}
+    </div>
+  </UseSortable>
+</template>
+```
+

   181	        // Traverse activeElement chain to find iframe, including through shadow DOMs
   182	        const { document: doc } = window
   183	        let activeElement: Element | null = doc.activeElement

   185	          if (activeElement.tagName === 'IFRAME') {

   187	            // doc.activeElement is the top-level element; if it's within the target,
   188	            // then the iframe is also within the target (even if in shadow DOM)
   189	            if (doc.activeElement !== activeElement) {

 # useFocusWithin

diff --git a/skills/vueuse-functions/references/useSortable.md b/skills/vueuse-functions/references/useSortable.md

@@ -96,6 +96,47 @@ useSortable('#dv', list)
 </template>
 ```
 
+### Using Component
+
+```vue
+<script setup lang="ts">
+import { UseSortable } from '@vueuse/integrations/useSortable/component'
+import { shallowRef } from 'vue'
+
+const list = shallowRef([
+  { id: 1, name: 'a' },
+  { id: 2, name: 'b' },
+  { id: 3, name: 'c' },
+])
+</script>
+
+<template>
+  <UseSortable v-model="list" as="ol" :options="{ animation: 150 }">
+    <li v-for="item in list" :key="item.id">
+      {{ item.name }}
+    </li>
+  </UseSortable>
+</template>
+```
+
+You can also access the helper functions like `start`, `stop`, and `option` from the slot scope:
+
+```vue
+<template>
+  <UseSortable v-slot="{ stop, start }" v-model="list">
+    <button @click="stop()">
+      Stop Sorting
+    </button>
+    <button @click="start()">
+      Start Sorting
+    </button>
+    <div v-for="item in list" :key="item.id">
+      {{ item.name }}
+    </div>
+  </UseSortable>
+</template>
+```
+
 ### Return Values
 
 | Property | Description                                                      |

 </template>
 ```
 
+### Using Component
+
+```vue
+<script setup lang="ts">
+import { UseSortable } from '@vueuse/integrations/useSortable/component'
+import { shallowRef } from 'vue'
+
+const list = shallowRef([
+  { id: 1, name: 'a' },
+  { id: 2, name: 'b' },
+  { id: 3, name: 'c' },
+])
+</script>
+
+<template>
+  <UseSortable v-model="list" as="ol" :options="{ animation: 150 }">
+    <li v-for="item in list" :key="item.id">
+      {{ item.name }}
+    </li>
+  </UseSortable>
+</template>
+```
+
+You can also access the helper functions like `start`, `stop`, and `option` from the slot scope:
+
+```vue
+<template>
+  <UseSortable v-slot="{ stop, start }" v-model="list">
+    <button @click="stop()">
+      Stop Sorting
+    </button>
+    <button @click="start()">
+      Start Sorting
+    </button>
+    <div v-for="item in list" :key="item.id">
+      {{ item.name }}
+    </div>
+  </UseSortable>
+</template>
+```
+
